\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and diagonal-base local exclusion]
\label{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}

and before

\begin{proposition}[Realization lemma for lifted germs]

\begin{lemma}[Centered tagged quintic witness survives specialization]
\label{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness}
On the tagged slice
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}),
\]
the first centered odd coefficient \(U_1\) of \(u_5(s)\) is nonzero. More
precisely,
\[
\delta u_1=0,\qquad \beta_0=0,
\qquad
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1,
\]
and the tagged slice contributes nontrivially to both factors
\[
v_0\neq 0,\qquad \delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
U_1\neq 0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package},
\[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr).
\]
Now specialize to the tagged slice \((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)})\) isolated in
Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}.

On that slice, the \(\eta_2\)-input in \(X_1\) is purely off-diagonal, so
\(u=w=0\) and therefore
\[
\delta u_1=0.
\]
Likewise, the \(q^{(5)}\)-input first appears only in the cubic same-point
coefficient \(G_3\), and there only in the diagonal sector; hence the induced
\(q^{(5)}\)-contribution to \(X_3\) is diagonal, so
\[
\beta_0=0.
\]
Thus
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1.
\]

Moreover, the explicit formula from Lemma~\ref{lem:quintic-trace-witness},
\[
v(h)=-\frac{1}{4\pi(s_1+s_2)}\,\eta_2(h),
\]
shows that the tagged \(\eta_2\)-slice contributes nontrivially to the even
coefficient \(v_0\). On the same tagged slice, the displayed linear
\(G_3\)-contribution to \(\gamma-\alpha\) in
Lemma~\ref{lem:quintic-trace-witness} has nonzero \(q^{(5)}\)-coefficient,
so the odd diagonal-difference coefficient \(\delta\alpha_1\) is nonzero.
Therefore
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1\neq 0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered quintic nontriviality]
\label{cor:centered-quintic-nontriviality}
On the centered diagonal branch one has
\[
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0.
\]
Consequently,
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S\not\equiv 0.
\]
In particular, the centered quintic pair cannot totally collapse:
\[
(u_5,v_5)\not\equiv (0,0).
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Lemma~\ref{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness} gives \(U_1\neq 0\), so
\(u_5(s)\) is a nonzero odd germ. The fixed-sector decomposition
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
and the linear independence of \(I,S\) imply that
\(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0\). Hence \((u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish
identically as a pair.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy on punctured arcs]
\label{cor:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch of the
underlying \(h\)-geometry. Then, after shrinking to one-sided punctured
neighborhoods of the centered base, either the branch lies in a good
\(v_5\)-patch
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
or else it lies in the parallel \(u_5\)-patch
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}
\]
from Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package},
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots,
\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
so \(c\neq 0\) near the centered base.

By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-nontriviality}, at least one of the two
odd germs \(u_5,v_5\) is nonzero. If \(v_5\not\equiv 0\), then its zeros are
isolated, so after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc we have
\(v_5\neq 0\). Along that arc,
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}.
\]
Since \(v_5/c\) is then a nonconstant analytic germ, \(M\) cannot vanish
identically on the arc. By analyticity, the zeros of \(M\) are isolated, so
after shrinking again one obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
which is exactly a good \(v_5\)-patch.

If instead \(v_5\equiv 0\), then Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-nontriviality}
forces \(u_5\not\equiv 0\). Since \(u_5\) is analytic, its zeros are isolated,
so after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} supplies the parallel
\(u_5\)-patch geometry there.
\end{proof}

This patch is the big one. It packages the centered U1U1​-witness, the pair-level nontriviality A5f≢0A5f​≡0, and the patch dichotomy that the mixed-side route really wants. It directly uses the existing quintic witness proof, the centered Taylor coefficients already in the draft, and the existing parallel u5u5​-patch remark.

\begin{proposition}[Linear independence of $1,u_5/c,v_5/c$]
\label{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}

and before

\begin{proposition}[Non-affinity of the lifted septic scalar]

\begin{corollary}[Automatic \(u_5\)-patch on a good \(M\neq 0\) interval]
\label{cor:automatic-u5-patch-on-good-M-interval}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval on which
\[
c\neq 0,
\qquad
M\neq 0.
\]
Then \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\). Consequently, every connected component of
\[
J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)
\]
is a valid local \(u_5\)-patch in the sense of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If \(u_5\equiv 0\) on \(J\), then the three functions
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
would be linearly dependent, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}. Thus
\(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\), so its zeros are isolated and each connected
component of \(J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)\) lies in \(\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}\).
The parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry then follows from
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{proof}

This captures the useful “fallback patch opens automatically once you are on any M≠0M=0 interval” consequence that came out of Route B and the existing linear-independence proposition.

\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]

\begin{remark}[Route B valuation tower and total-collapse degeneration]
\label{rem:route-b-valuation-tower-total-collapse}
Write
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,
\qquad
\ord_s v_5=2r+1,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
If \(\lambda\) is analytic odd and \(r\ge m\), then
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge \ord_s v_5-\ord_s u_5+1
=2(r-m)+1.
\]

Indeed, if
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}=2d+1<2(r-m)+1,
\]
then
\[
\ord_s(u_5v_{7,K_1})=(2m+1)+(2d+1)\le 2r,
\]
while
\[
\ord_s(u_{7,K_1}v_5)\ge 1+(2r+1)=2r+2,
\]
contradicting
\[
\ord_s\Delta_7\ge 2r+2,
\]
which follows from \(\Delta_7=\lambda\,v_5\) with \(\lambda\) odd.

In particular, if
\[
V_1=\cdots=V_{2r-1}=0,
\qquad
U_{2m+1}\neq 0,
\qquad
V_{2r+1}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat V_1=\cdots=\widehat V_{2(r-m)-1}=0,
\]
and the first potentially surviving coupled coefficient is
\[
D_{2r+2}
=
\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}
-
U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\]

Moreover, if the centered quintic pair collapses identically,
\[
u_5\equiv 0,\qquad v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then automatically
\[
\Delta_7\equiv 0,
\]
and the centered source formulas give the germ-level linear system
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}=0.
\]
Hence either
\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv \delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]

So the failure of the \(v_5\)-route is not an isolated coefficient accident.
It forces either a triangular coupled quintic--septic degeneration tower, or a
full source-level degeneration of the centered quintic transport package.
\end{remark}

This captures the real structural “goodies” from Route B: the valuation theorem, the first-surviving D2r+2D2r+2​ formula, and the total-collapse linear system.

\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected interaction remainder with the required swap
symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal collapse identities, so that the
quadratic factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
becomes automatic.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local repeated-node three-point branch is already classified. What remains
is global continuation / recurrence control for the unique odd-order branch and
the exclusion of infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch via centered quintic-patch dichotomy.}
The centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now the correct pair-level object. If the centered tagged quintic witness
survives specialization so that
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
then one-sided punctured arcs must enter either a good \(v_5\)-patch or the
parallel \(u_5\)-patch. On the \(v_5\)-patch side, the centered-to-patch bridge
then controls the explicit mixed low-order bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed branch via deeper RH-specific identities.}
Generic local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets,
so the next theorem there is not a blanket sterility statement but a deeper
RH-specific parity / divisibility theorem forcing extra vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently of the nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]

\item
\textbf{Route B backup degeneration tower.}
If the \(v_5\)-patch fails, the valuation theorem for
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}
\]
forces matching late vanishing in the septic transport channel, and total
centered quintic collapse forces a source-level degeneration. Thus the failure
of the \(v_5\)-route is already confined to a narrow coupled degeneration
scheme rather than a free local cancellation.

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no definitive local closure can come
from the lifted variables alone, any final \(4\)-point closure theorem must
ultimately come from deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, for
example a witness-transport lemma for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) or an RH-specific
divisibility / parity identity for
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

This replacement aligns the “main route” with the quintic-patch dichotomy and demotes raw V1V1​-chasing to backup status, which matches where the chat ended up.

Insert:

\begin{corollary}[Automatic \(u_5\)-patch on a good \(M\neq 0\) interval]
\label{cor:automatic-u5-patch-on-good-M-interval}
Let \(J\) be a connected open interval on which
\[
c\neq 0,
\qquad
M\neq 0.
\]
Then \(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\). Consequently, every connected component of
\[
J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)
\]
is a valid local \(u_5\)-patch in the sense of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If \(u_5\equiv 0\) on \(J\), then the three functions
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
would be linearly dependent, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}. Thus
\(u_5\not\equiv 0\) on \(J\), so its zeros are isolated and each connected
component of \(J\setminus u_5^{-1}(0)\) lies in \(\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0\}\).
The parallel \(u_5\)-patch geometry then follows from
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}.
\end{proof}

Why: this makes explicit a structural finding that is currently only implicit in the combination of the linear-independence proposition and the parallel u5u5​-patch remark. It strengthens the fallback geometry story in a useful, theorem-level way.

\begin{remark}[Determinant-level parity on a centered good patch]
\label{rem:determinant-level-parity-centered-good-patch}

Yes. Here is the draft-ready version I would use.

I’d actually formulate it as a pair: a main local trichotomy lemma, then a short corollary saying the only genuinely new branch left for the mixed analysis is the clean V1≠0V1​=0 branch.
Main lemma

\begin{lemma}[Local trichotomy for the mixed branch near the centered base]
\label{lem:local-trichotomy-mixed-branch-centered-base}
Assume the centered branch is in the centered symmetric-placement regime, and
assume the centered tagged quintic witness gives
\[
U_1\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+\cdots
\]
has a simple odd zero at the centered base, so with
\[
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),
\qquad
C_0\neq 0,
\]
the \(u_5\)-patch coordinate
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base.

Let
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then every sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point branch falls into exactly
one of the following three local regimes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] \textbf{Clean \(v_5\)-branch:}
\[
\ord_s v_5=1.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
v_5(s)=V_1s+V_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
V_1\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots,
\qquad
X_1=\frac{V_1}{C_0}\neq 0,
\]
so \(x=v_5/c\) is an odd local coordinate and the branch lies locally in a
genuine good \(v_5\)-patch.

\item[(ii)] \textbf{Late \(v_5\)-branch with nontrivial \(u_5\)-patch lift:}
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3,
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0.
\]
Then \(x(y)\) and \(\widetilde\tau_u(y)\) are odd germs, and
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\qquad
\ord_0 x\ge 3,
\qquad
\ord_0 \widetilde\tau_u\ge 3.
\]
After an ambient coordinate permutation
\[
(y,x,\widetilde\tau_u)\mapsto (x,y,\widetilde\tau_u)
\]
and, if needed, subtraction of a suitable odd multiple to separate equal
leading odd orders, the germ reduces to the odd/odd local normal form
\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
n>m\ge 3,
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
or to a simpler degenerate case with one higher-order channel identically zero.

\item[(iii)] \textbf{Residual planar-lift corner:}
\[
\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3,
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0.
\]
Then \(\tau_u(y)=a\,y\) for some constant \(a\), equivalently
\[
-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]
In this case
\[
Q_u=(y,x,ay),
\]
so after the ambient shear
\[
(Y,X,Z)\mapsto (Y,X,Z-aY)
\]
the lifted \(u_5\)-patch curve becomes
\[
Q_u\sim (y,x,0),
\]
hence is affine-planar.
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Because \(U_1\neq 0\), the germ \(u_5(s)\) has order \(1\), hence
\[
y=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate.

Since \(v_5\) is odd on the centered branch, either \(\ord_s v_5=1\) or
\(\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3\) is odd. This gives the dichotomy between (i) and
the late-\(v_5\) cases (ii)--(iii).

In case (i),
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}=X_1s+X_3s^3+\cdots
\]
with \(X_1=V_1/C_0\neq 0\), so \(x\) is an odd local coordinate. Moreover,
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2},
\]
hence
\[
M(0)=c(0)^2x'(0)=C_0V_1\neq 0,
\]
so the branch lies locally in a genuine good \(v_5\)-patch.

Now assume \(\ord_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3\). Because \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even,
\[
x(y)=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is odd, with
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(\ord_0 x\ge 3\). Also \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\)
is odd, hence
\[
\tau_u(y)=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
is odd. Therefore \(\widetilde\tau_u(y)=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)y\) is odd and
either vanishes identically or has odd order at least \(3\).

If \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\), then after the stated ambient coordinate
permutation and, if needed, subtraction of a suitable odd multiple to separate
equal leading odd orders, the germ reduces to the displayed odd/odd local
normal form, yielding (ii).

If \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\), then \(\tau_u(y)=a\,y\) for some constant
\(a\), which is equivalent to
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]
Then
\[
Q_u=(y,x,ay),
\]
and the stated ambient shear makes the third coordinate vanish identically,
yielding the planar-lift form (iii).
\end{proof}

Corollary that says what this buys you

\begin{corollary}[Local reduction of the mixed branch near the centered base]
\label{cor:local-reduction-mixed-branch-centered-base}
Assume the odd/odd local sterility theorem applies to the normalized odd/odd
model in Lemma~\ref{lem:local-trichotomy-mixed-branch-centered-base}(ii). Then
every sufficiently small nearby mixed \(4\)-point obstruction branch near the
centered base is reduced to one of the following two possibilities:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] the clean branch \(\ord_s v_5=1\), on which the good \(v_5\)-patch is
already open locally and the remaining task is the finite-jet parity transfer
in
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c};
\]

\item[(b)] the planar-lift corner
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\]
on the \(u_5\)-patch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:local-trichotomy-mixed-branch-centered-base}, every
sufficiently small nearby mixed branch falls into one of the three regimes
(i)--(iii). Regime (ii) reduces to the odd/odd local normal form already known
to be punctured-neighborhood sterile, so it cannot support a nearby mixed
obstruction branch. The only remaining possibilities are (i) and (iii).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Right-pincer \(u_5\)-patch transplant]
